  632. # [05:04] <dev> but what confused me then, is how does firefox show me the "hey this JS is sucking and taking too much time"

  647. # [05:07] <dev> so if I am doing an sync XHR to the same url a.com/foo from 2 different tabs (b.com and c.com), then the two XHRs can't race?
  648. # [05:10] <khuey> what do you mean race?
  649. # [05:10] <khuey> if the second one starts before the first one finishes
  650. # [05:10] <khuey> not only can the second one finish first
  651. # [05:10] <khuey> the second one *will* finish first
  652. # [05:12] <njn> RyanVM: windows bustage? dammit. Sorry

  654. # [05:15] <khuey> dev: well sure, but even ignoring XHR for the moment
  655. # [05:15] * Quits: rjohnson19 (chatzilla@moz-9148485F.hsd1.ma.comcast.net) (Quit: ChatZilla 0.9.88-rdmsoft [XULRunner 1.9.0.17/2009122204])
  656. # [05:15] <khuey> dev: there's nothing that ensures that the responses are received in the same order they leave the server
  657. # [05:15] * Joins: ekr_ (ekr@moz-1515ED18.mycingular.net)
  658. # [05:15] <khuey> dev: if these are entirely separate http connections
  659. # [05:16] <dev> yeah, but since it is a sync XHR; whichever tab got to run first will complete before the second gets to make a request
  660. # [05:16] <khuey> dev: no
  661. # [05:16] <khuey> dev: it's only "sync" in the since that it prevents the currently executing JS from continuing
  662. # [05:16] <khuey> dev: it doesn't block other pages from proceeding
  663. # [05:16] <dev> ohh
  664. # [05:16] <dev> hmm wait
  665. # [05:17] <dev> so what does "Everything runs in same thread" mean .. I thought that meant there was one global event loop for JS events across tabs
  666. # [05:18] <khuey> there is
  667. # [05:18] <khuey> so, here's how sync XHR works
  668. # [05:18] <khuey> a web page calls XHR.send on a sync XHR
  669. # [05:18] <khuey> the C stack looks something like
  670. # [05:18] <khuey> nsXMLHttpRequest::Send
  671. # [05:18] <khuey> JS
  672. # [05:18] <khuey> more JS
  673. # [05:18] <khuey> etc
  674. # [05:19] * Quits: nhirata (nhirata.bu@moz-6D599AA6.hsd1.ca.comcast.net) (Ping timeout)
  675. # [05:19] * Quits: jwilde (Earlybird@moz-BBE3ABD.mv.mozilla.com) (Ping timeout)
  676. # [05:19] <dev> (I am with you .. I didn't want to interrupt the middle of your explanation)
  677. # [05:19] <khuey> eventually we end up at http://mxr.mozilla.org/mozilla-central/source/content/base/src/nsXMLHttpRequest.cpp#3162
  678. # [05:19] <khuey> and we start "spinning" the event loop
  679. # [05:20] <khuey> and that can run a timeout or a load event or whatever for page 2
  680. # [05:20] <khuey> so then the C stack looks like
  681. # [05:20] <khuey> page 2 JS
  682. # [05:20] <khuey> NS_ProcessNextEvent
  683. # [05:20] <khuey> nsXMLHttpRequest::Send
  684. # [05:20] <khuey> page 1 JS
  685. # [05:20] <khuey> more JS
  686. # [05:20] <khuey> if page 2 starts a sync XHR, you end up with
  687. # [05:20] <khuey> NS_ProcessNextEvent
  688. # [05:21] <khuey> nsXMLHttpRequest::Send
  689. # [05:21] <khuey> page 2 JS
  690. # [05:21] <khuey> NS_ProcessNextEvent
  691. # [05:21] <khuey> nsXMLHttpRequest::Send
  692. # [05:21] <khuey> page 1 JS
  693. # [05:21] <khuey> more JS
  694. # [05:21] <khuey> so the problem here is that if page 1's XHR completes
  695. # [05:21] <khuey> there's no way to resume executing page 1's script before page 2's XHR completes
  696. # [05:22] <khuey> so regardless of what order the responses are received in, page 2 will appear to finish first
  697. # [05:22] <dev> aah ok
  698. # [05:22] <khuey> make sense?
  699. # [05:23] <dev> so the way I look at it, when a developer makes a sync XHR (s)he hasn't really finished handling the event, and so NS_ProcessNextEvent can't, e.g., process an event on the same page
  700. # [05:23] <dev> right?
  701. # [05:23] * Quits: gozala (gozala@moz-D5BED6F9.dsl.dynamic.sonic.net) (Ping timeout)
  702. # [05:23] <khuey> well, it can in certain cases
  703. # [05:23] <khuey> but those are bugs
  704. # [05:23] <dev> yeah
  705. # [05:23] * Joins: tn (tn@8F761026.B5EF4AF6.E96CA9D8.IP)
  706. # [05:23] <khuey> we try to suppress running any additional script from page 1 while this is ongoing
  707. # [05:24] <khuey> you can see some of the logic around that call
  708. # [05:24] * nical|away is now known as nical
  709. # [05:24] <dev> so if you call this current sync XHR thing as "calling NS_ProcessNextEvent" in the middle of an event handler, is the only place this could happen sync XHR or are there other places ?
  710. # [05:24] * Joins: ekr__ (ekr@moz-A62EC22B.hfc.comcastbusiness.net)

  714. # [05:25] <khuey> dev: e.g. alert()
  715. # [05:25] <benjamin> http://mxr.mozilla.org/mozilla-central/ident?i=NS_ProcessNextEvent ...

  717. # [05:26] * Quits: jgilbert (jgilbert@F2D29657.F60B0462.67AC9B1.IP) (Ping timeout)
  718. # [05:26] <dev> ok.. so this is starting to make sense now.
  719. # [05:27] <khuey> dev: so this situation where you have some blocked page JS and a processnextevent call is called a "nested" event loop

  730. # [05:31] <khuey> dev: well sync XHR in workers is different

  737. # [05:32] * Quits: ekr_ (ekr@moz-1515ED18.mycingular.net) (Quit: Colloquy for iPhone - http://colloquy.mobi)
